  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3cf205e0-33a8-46b3-b574-eefdd9582ecf'
      });
    }

With the help of The Keeper and the Fron army, Owen has managed to buy some time, but new problems have already emerged, new secrets need to be revealed, and the race against time to stop Them from conquering both dimensions has only just begun. The Keeper, Owen Sage, and his friends at Easton Falls University must now battle threats from within. To do it, they must reunite with familiar creatures and join forces with new ones as they navigate their journey to the truth that awaits them in Everville.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

<div id="review_717341291" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/717341291" />
    <a title="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews"><img alt="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346883958p2/12558730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/717341291?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" href="/user/show/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews">M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer717341291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11554306942893053211">The first book in this series was a bit vague, but the second book really helps to flesh out the series and explore the world of Everville more. On its own, the first book was a bit weak, but after reading this book, I can definitely appreciate and understand the world of Everville more, so I will give this book 5 stars.<br/><br/>There are seven Pillars, and at the end of the first book and this one, Owen encounters a Pillar, and is given a question/test. We also learn more about the villains. Given that </span>
  <span id="freeText11554306942893053211" style="display:none">The first book in this series was a bit vague, but the second book really helps to flesh out the series and explore the world of Everville more. On its own, the first book was a bit weak, but after reading this book, I can definitely appreciate and understand the world of Everville more, so I will give this book 5 stars.<br /><br />There are seven Pillars, and at the end of the first book and this one, Owen encounters a Pillar, and is given a question/test. We also learn more about the villains. Given that there are five Pillars left for Owen to be tested by, I think I can safely surmise there will be five more books. These two books already out are kind of like puzzle pieces, with each book filling in more of a picture, so I am eager to see the rest of the picture, since the author has some really creative ideas, this is a series very different than anything I've read before, and I am definitely eager to read the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11554306942893053211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer775887677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13643576166619809684">A thrilling story with a lesson for YA readers!<br/><br/>"One lesson you have yet to learn, Owen, is that sometimes it's okay to take time to enjoy what's important, and to see what makes up the wonderful world in which you live."<br/>Very nice, fast-paced, thrilling and mesmerizing YA fiction, including superb fantasy and sci-fi.<br/>This 2nd book of the Everville series lived up to our expectations and even surpassed them. I was really glad to read the Keeper's or the author's wise psychological insights at the e</span>
  <span id="freeText13643576166619809684" style="display:none">A thrilling story with a lesson for YA readers!<br /><br />"One lesson you have yet to learn, Owen, is that sometimes it's okay to take time to enjoy what's important, and to see what makes up the wonderful world in which you live."<br />Very nice, fast-paced, thrilling and mesmerizing YA fiction, including superb fantasy and sci-fi.<br />This 2nd book of the Everville series lived up to our expectations and even surpassed them.   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/986246001?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" href="/user/show/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya">Anna (Enchanted by YA)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer986246001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6013935353262598977"><i>***I received the eBook free as a review copy from the author in exchange for an honest review***</i><br/><br/>I’m still under the impression that this series has a lot of potential, but once again I don’t think it met it quite yet.<br/><br/>This book while still focused around Owen, spent a lot of time doing character as well as world development elsewhere. New characters were introduced left right and centre, and I’d only just got a feel for Owen and his friends so it didn’t work for me.<br/><br/>Huff’s writing has always been</span>
  <span id="freeText6013935353262598977" style="display:none"><i>***I received the eBook free as a review copy from the author in exchange for an honest review***</i><br /><br />I’m still under the impression that this series has a lot of potential, but once again I don’t think it met it quite yet.<br /><br />This book while still focused around Owen, spent a lot of time doing character as well as world development elsewhere. New characters were introduced left right and centre, and I’d only just got a feel for Owen and his friends so it didn’t work for me.<br /><br />Huff’s writing has always been filled with long and detailed descriptions, this book was no exception, and although it made sure you knew exactly what was going on and where, it made me feel more detached than it has previously and I felt a lot more like a bystander to the story than living it.<br /><br />Something that I’d consider an impressive feat, was how even with these descriptions he was able to weave a lesson into the story. It’s subtle but the way it comes into play in the plot also makes it powerful. Owen has to make some important choices in this book that can shape a lot more than just his life at that moment, so to teach the importance of all decisions and their outcomes whether they affect only that day or the rest of their lives and who they become is a great thing.<br /><br />Posted on: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">http://enchantedbyya.blogspot.co.uk/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6013935353262598977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_630353614" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/630353614" />
    <a title="Monica Reents" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13910930-monica-reents"><img alt="Monica Reents" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525921392p2/13910930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/630353614?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monica Reents" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monica Reents" href="/user/show/13910930-monica-reents">Monica Reents</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer630353614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9191490985991569896">The Everville YA saga continues with The City of Worms. I have been fortunate to receive an advanced copy of this book in edited draft form, from Roy Huff, to read and review. I was more than willing to oblige since I find this series fascinating. The adventures have continued with the same excitement we anticipated after reading The First Pillar. You find yourself immersed into other worlds with unique characters in a battle of good v. evil. <br/><br/>The authors’ descriptive language allows the reader t</span>
  <span id="freeText9191490985991569896" style="display:none">The Everville YA saga continues with The City of Worms. I have been fortunate to receive an advanced copy of this book in edited draft form, from Roy Huff, to read and review. I was more than willing to oblige since I find this series fascinating. The adventures have continued with the same excitement we anticipated after reading The First Pillar. You find yourself immersed into other worlds with unique characters in a battle of good v. evil. <br /><br />The authors’ descriptive language allows the reader to delve right into the story and be transported from Everville to The Earthly Realm to The Other InBetween lands along with Owen and The Keeper. You will meet unforgettable characters and races; such as, The Marmooks, The Fron, The Giants, Ubaloo, The Fwaylan, Toe, The Keeper, Zee, Anika, Owen, Dante, Oldrik, Them…just to name a few. <br /><br />Owen is a strong main character. He makes a great leader and he is willing to do what is necessary to win this battle; he is not the only one who feels this way so secrets are discovered and loyalties are questioned. Where Owen found confusion in his role of helping Everville and the earthly realm battle their enemy, he now understands and knows what must be done and is ready, with the help of his friends, to do whatever he must to save Dante’s life and win this battle. <br /><br />I thought that the battle scenes were well written and thought out and have the ability to put the reader on the battlefield with the characters. <br /><br />This series is creatively written and I feel that Roy Huff’s imagination for fantasy writing is superb. The characters are fully developed, as is the storyline. This book is a fun and interesting read with surprises, twists, and turns. It will keep you turning the pages and trying to guess what could possibly happen next…compelling you to read through to the last word. I recommend this book to everyone who enjoys a creatively, smart written fantasy novel. Roy Huff’s series will keep you entertained from the first to the last word and I look forward to the adventures that his future books hold. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9191490985991569896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15987813152930071993" style="display:none">Rather than diving right in and giving one of those extensive, in-depth reviews that discloses the Story and then get the Reviewer's thoughts and opinions, I stay with just the opinion.<br /><br />Somehow all the 'rage' is vampire, werewolf, or brain-eating mutant creature(s).       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2236983-sandra-stiles?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer753720872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8466492488818075669">I loved visiting with these characters again. The author held true to the first story creating new characters that within the world of fantasy are very believable. One of my students told me the other day that she liked reading books that was more like turning a movie on in her brain. I know exactly what she was talking about. This author is wonderful at creating that movie in your brain. His descriptions of characters and the battles are a real treat for a visual person like me.<br/><br/>Another thing I </span>
  <span id="freeText8466492488818075669" style="display:none">I loved visiting with these characters again. The author held true to the first story creating new characters that within the world of fantasy are very believable. One of my students told me the other day that she liked reading books that was more like turning a movie on in her brain. I know exactly what she was talking about. This author is wonderful at creating that movie in your brain. His descriptions of characters and the battles are a real treat for a visual person like me.<br /><br />Another thing I really enjoyed was the way a lesson was woven into the story without coming across as preachy. In school we are always teaching our middle schoolers that the decisions they make today will affect their lives and the person they become for a long time. This book carries that same message. Owen has to make some tough decisions that carry some very have effects for the future.<br /><br />I used to say I didn't like reading fantasy. However, if you were to check my shelves at school, the fantasy section makes up at least a quarter of all of my books. That would be somewhere around 300 to 350 fantasy books. What I discovered was that I don't care for adult fantasy books. I love middle grade and young adult fantasy. This one is a great addition to my school shelves, and one that I recommend to all fantasy lovers.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17797789204035774644">Everville: The City of Worms by Roy Huff is the second book in the Everville series and like the first book it will grab you by the seat of your pants and keep you glued to the story. This YA adventure is full of action and intrigue.<br/><br/>The author did a great job of continuing to develop the Everville storyline and the transition from book one to this book was seamless.   <span id="freeText17797789204035774644" style="display:none">Everville: The City of Worms by Roy Huff is the second book in the Everville series and like the first book it will grab you by the seat of your pants and keep you glued to the story. This YA adventure is full of action and intrigue.<br /><br />The author did a great job of continuing to develop the Everville storyline and the transition from book one to this book was seamless. I really enjoyed the way the author developed multiple plot lines with constant twist and turns which kept me hooked. Even with all the plot twist it was easy to keep up and Roy Huff brought it all together for an exciting conclusion. But, he set the stage for the next book in the series.<br /><br />I really liked the way Roy Huff developed each of his characters. They are real and very believable. It was easy to follow along and place yourself into the story as a silent partner. I liked the way the heroes of the story had depth and were easy to identify with.<br /><br />I really enjoyed Everville: The City of Worms by Roy Huff and I highly recommend this book to all readers.<br /><br /><br />[Please note: I was given a free copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.]<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9859885868075302290">I was impressed by this book. Continuing on from the first book in the series, Roy Huff has once again proved his talent for building unforgettable settings and highly original creatures to inhabit them.<br/><br/>I liked the character progression I saw in this book. From the first story the main character has grown a lot and we were able to see him more three dimensionally this time around. I found the dialogue engaging and the plot moved forward in ways that I had not expected. <br/><br/>One thing that is truly re</span>
  <span id="freeText9859885868075302290" style="display:none">I was impressed by this book. Continuing on from the first book in the series, Roy Huff has once again proved his talent for building unforgettable settings and highly original creatures to inhabit them.<br /><br />I liked the character progression I saw in this book. From the first story the main character has grown a lot and we were able to see him more three dimensionally this time around. I found the dialogue engaging and the plot moved forward in ways that I had not expected. <br /><br />One thing that is truly remarkable about this series, and this book in particular, is the way the author draws the reader into the story right along with the characters. Whilst reading Roy Huff's work, you don't feel like a simple bystander, but rather that you are getting the opportunity to experience what the characters are experiencing and go along for the journey with them. <br /><br />Some of the simple logistics issues I had with the first book were worked out int his one. This was a smooth ride with no bumps along the way. <br /><br />Th ending of this book was very well written and I am now excited to read the third installment. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/717412631" />
    <a title="Sherry Ellis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5262608-sherry-ellis"><img alt="Sherry Ellis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302699048p2/5262608.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/717412631?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sherry Ellis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sherry Ellis" href="/user/show/5262608-sherry-ellis">Sherry Ellis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer717412631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2757870565916810463">City of Worms is the second book in the Everville series. Protagonist, Owen Sage, a college student, is once again battling the forces of evil. The antagonistic Them are trying to invade the idyllic world of Everville. It's up to Owen and his friends to stop the Them. The story oscillates between Everville, The Earthly Realm, and The Other In Between lands. There is an impressive cast of characters from such creatures known as Marmooks, From, and Ubaloo. Some readers may find it challenging to k</span>
  <span id="freeText2757870565916810463" style="display:none">City of Worms is the second book in the Everville series. Protagonist, Owen Sage, a college student, is once again battling the forces of evil. The antagonistic Them are trying to invade the idyllic world of Everville. It's up to Owen and his friends to stop the Them. The story oscillates between Everville, The Earthly Realm, and The Other In Between lands. There is an impressive cast of characters from such creatures known as Marmooks, From, and Ubaloo. Some readers may find it challenging to keep it all straight in their heads, especially if they haven't read the first book.<br /><br />The biggest strength of this book is the descriptive writing, which allows readers to visualize the action. It is particularly good in the description of the City of Worms and the final battle scene. But be prepared to feel the need to purchase the next installment in the series, as the cliffhanger at the end leaves the reader wanting more.<br /><br />If you are a fan of YA fantasy, this imaginative story is probably one you will enjoy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2757870565916810463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1309666498226431424" style="display:none">A thrilling story with a lesson for YA readers!<br /><br />"One lesson you have yet to learn, Owen, is that sometimes it's okay to take time to enjoy what's important, and to see what makes up the wonderful world in which you live."<br />Very nice, fast-paced, thrilling and mesmerizing YA fiction, including superb fantasy and sci-fi.<br />This 2nd book of the Everville series lived up to our expectations and even surpassed them.   <span id="freeText5849943933560939117" style="display:none"><i>Everville ~ The City of Worms</i> is the second book in the series and Owen, a college student continues as the main character and leader in the fight of good against evil. The battle descriptions put the reader in the middle of the action in this parallel world with an interesting group of other world creatures. Roy Huff's ability to make them seem real makes this a great fantasy. Exciting from beginning to end, it leaves the reader wanting to find out what will happen in the next episode for Everville. Fantasy lovers this is a must read, as the descriptions of the fantasy world is top notch.</span>

<div id="review_718656115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/718656115" />
    <a title="Wendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16831198-wendy"><img alt="Wendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396967875p2/16831198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/718656115?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/16831198-wendy">Wendy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">1</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Wendy by: </span>
      Sequel
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16831198-wendy?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16831198-wendy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer718656115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14038766096037313945">The second installment in the Everville saga, " The City of Worms" is as mesmerizing and imaginative as Roy Huff's first book, The First Pillar." In this sequel Anika and Owen's friend Dante lies in a coma in the earthly realm, his fate linked to magical artifacts that have to be destroyed, while in Everville the traitorous Oldrik and his three accomplices have escaped their captors to join forces with the evil darkness that lurks in the Other In Between. With them go Fron secrets that could mak</span>
  <span id="freeText14038766096037313945" style="display:none">The second installment in the Everville saga, " The City of Worms" is as mesmerizing and imaginative as Roy Huff's first book, The First Pillar." In this sequel Anika and Owen's friend Dante lies in a coma in the earthly realm, his fate linked to magical artifacts that have to be destroyed, while in Everville the traitorous Oldrik and his three accomplices have escaped their captors to join forces with the evil darkness that lurks in the Other In Between. With them go Fron secrets that could make Them more powerful than anyone could imagine. But this is only the start of an adventure that brings a clash of armies as the dark horde seeks power, and a summons to Owen to help unravel a secret at the Second Pillar that could mean life or death for the realms. Will Dante recover? Will the Keeper, Owen Sage and his friends be able to save both dimensions from evil's onslaught? The answers to these questions and more lie at the heart of a novel that brings heightened tension and anticipation as the characters battle new threats.<br /><br />As well as encountering familiar creatures in this story, Roy Huff brings to life new ones who are just as original and fascinating as the short, thick, hairless Fron and the furry headed marmooks. The Ubaloo are twelve inch, muscular warriors who will fight alongside a Giant army lead by the brave Bardok, and General Varrick and his Frons face a new enemy, the dark winged Fwalyn their teeth and claws eager to shred flesh. <br /><br />In this novel the characters' personalities evolve as they face new challenges. Owen Sage is not only smart and brave, but also shows humility and wisdom in his decisions. Anika gravitates between apprehension and depression while Dante's hospitalized, and shows little compassion or thought for Zee's feelings when she plans a party for the recovered patient. A confused Cleophas suffering from bouts of memory loss is determined to fight the evil invading the earthly realm even after he courageously hands over his leadership to Avery. In Everville the fortitude and determination of the Fron, the Keeper, and two of the repentant traitors-Elmer and Calvin -are unforgettable as are their nemeses; the arrogant, conniving, abusive Oldrik, the contemptible, proud Jacob, and the power-hungry turncoat Mallory.<br /><br />Well-written, the plot steadily moves from one conflict to the next as it explores values like friendship, self-sacrifice, and commitment amidst the chaos and violence that besets the realms where good and evil coexist. I enjoyed this novel as much as the first, and look forward to reading about further exploits.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14038766096037313945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_588045312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/588045312" />
    <a title="BJ  Almeda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15886575-bj-almeda"><img alt="BJ  Almeda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373989909p2/15886575.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/588045312?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BJ  Almeda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BJ  Almeda" href="/user/show/15886575-bj-almeda">BJ  Almeda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer588045312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16140161194729177084">What can I say?<br/>The second book was as magical and as fantastic as the first book.<br/>Roy has still this good eye for descriptions and a wide mind for imaginations. Everything was in order and everything was so captivating. You can really see it in your eyes, what was happening. You can, especially, intricately picture out the images that Roy wants you to see. That is a very good point for an author. It was not boring at all.<br/><br/>What made me like the book so much is that it was, this time, mostly, action</span>
  <span id="freeText16140161194729177084" style="display:none">What can I say?<br />The second book was as magical and as fantastic as the first book.<br />Roy has still this good eye for descriptions and a wide mind for imaginations. Everything was in order and everything was so captivating. You can really see it in your eyes, what was happening. You can, especially, intricately picture out the images that Roy wants you to see. That is a very good point for an author. It was not boring at all.<br /><br />What made me like the book so much is that it was, this time, mostly, action and adventure. There was no resting point in this book. My heart always skips a beat.<br /><br />CHARACTERS<br />Owen was still the Owen that we knew. He is still this charming kid who is always taken to Everville by the keeper. Then there's Anika who is just as loving as ever. She loves her friends so much. hmm..Then Dante, if you can haven't read the first book, Dante was in a state of Coma because of helping Owen by channeling his energy to help in the war against Them.<br /><br />What I love about the characters is that they are so captivating (I say this in a lot of my reviews). Captivating characters means true characters. You feel them.<br /><br />You can feel that he someone is really bad because of the way they are pictured in the book- how they act, talk and grin. haha! You can see their evil faces when they do that or when the author says so.<br /><br />THE PLOT<br />With Roy's awesome skills, he delivered a well arranged and well thought plot. It is not topsy-turvy like some books where some parts should be placed before or after a certain part.<br /><br />HOWEVER.<br /><br />I have minor issues about the book. One is the writing (this is different from the descriptions, okay?) . There are times that I noticed that there are some misplaced modifiers, if you know what I mean. That's not so obvious but that is still gramatically wrong. hmm.. but you can still get it, you still enjoy the book.<br /><br />OVER ALL,<br /><br />I really enjoyed and loved the book. I am looking forward to book 3. </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/628374251?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1042664891307463216">Exclusive Review : The City of Worms (Everville #2)<br/>I happen to be among the lucky few who got to proof read the book! I thank the writer Roy Huff for it. <br/>And before I get to the Review : SPOILER ALERT!<br/><br/>The story picks off from the last book (The First Pillar (Everville #1)) - With Owen and Fron winning the first battle and Dante going to a vegetative state as an unexpected consequence. Owen's mission now seems to be fighting the evil Them who are determined more than ever before and repairing the</span>
  <span id="freeText1042664891307463216" style="display:none">Exclusive Review : The City of Worms (Everville #2)<br />I happen to be among the lucky few who got to proof read the book! I thank the writer Roy Huff for it. <br />And before I get to the Review : SPOILER ALERT!<br /><br />The story picks off from the last book (The First Pillar (Everville #1)) - With Owen and Fron winning the first battle and Dante going to a vegetative state as an unexpected consequence. Owen's mission now seems to be fighting the evil Them who are determined more than ever before and repairing the breach.<br /><br />The writer,as promised has answered as to why Owen and his friends were in first place were chosen to restore the balance between good and evil and repair the breach. Owen now clearly knows who his "Friends" and who his "Enemies" are. <br />I can safely say the writer has matured since his last book. <br /><br />The story line essentially emphasizes on a very basic fact that our choices dictate the person who we really are - Good or Evil. The protagonists of this book seem to be delivering that message bang on.<br /><br />The book ends with a magnificent battle as anticipated with Them and armies of Giants, Forn and Owen , where in Owen is forced to take a major decision with a result of a new stronger and meaner enemy being born (I really don't want to give away any more details! Read the book!) <br /><br />The climax of the book really surprised me. Its a perfectly unexpected twist for a plot that was near predictable till that twist came along.<br /><br />Roy again has done a fantastic job in describing the City of Worms and the Battle. I was able to visualize the battle perfectly for the description was written passion. Worth being made into a movie (Though with a little more effects and twists to the plot!) <br /><br />I'd give the Book 4.2 on 5.</span>

<div id="review_654995840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/654995840" />
    <a title="Jonel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15432163-jonel"><img alt="Jonel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476629586p2/15432163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/654995840?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonel" href="/user/show/15432163-jonel">Jonel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer654995840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2631227590386456971">This was a very well written novel that is thought provoking and intensely enjoyable. Right from the beginning, Huff is drawing his audience in. He gives just enough background information to jog your memory as to the events of the 1st book in the series without rehashing anything. This is a fluid novel that transitions seamlessly from one section to the next. Fantasy creatures abound. They are all well developed as species and some as individuals. Huff also gives more background information on </span>
  <span id="freeText2631227590386456971" style="display:none">This was a very well written novel that is thought provoking and intensely enjoyable. Right from the beginning, Huff is drawing his audience in. He gives just enough background information to jog your memory as to the events of the 1st book in the series without rehashing anything. This is a fluid novel that transitions seamlessly from one section to the next. Fantasy creatures abound. They are all well developed as species and some as individuals. Huff also gives more background information on Everville in this instalment. It really helps to round out your experience of the story. Intrigue and suspense also make an appearance in this magically crafted world. Huff’s vividly visual descriptions draw you in and his intriguing storyline keep you there. He definitely takes the fantasy genre and gives it an exciting twist.<br /><br />The characters that we came to know and love in the 1st book continue to grow as individuals. The names of the characters in this novel make me giggle but are definitely memorable. They are also well suited to the characters themselves. In all actuality, they add to the characters and definitely stick in your mind. In all honesty, this novel has a rather large cast of characters but they are easy to keep straight. Some are developed as individuals and others as groups. This gives a very intriguing contrast to the characters.<br /><br />Overall, this is a story that makes your imagination soar. It was an extremely enjoyable read and a definite must for all those who enjoy the YA fantasy genre. Holy cliffanger though. This novel definitely leaves you needing the sequel. <br /><br />Please note that I received this novel free of charge from the author in exchange for an honest review.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2631227590386456971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1309330134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1309330134" />
    <a title="Clare O&#39;Beara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23233462-clare-o-beara"><img alt="Clare O&#39;Beara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585485276p2/23233462.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1309330134?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clare O&#39;Beara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clare O&#39;Beara" href="/user/show/23233462-clare-o-beara">Clare O&#39;Beara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23233462-clare-o-beara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1309330134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18115615006023357275">I found myself at a severe disadvantage by not having read the earlier book in the fantasy series. No information is presented in the first quarter, which is as far as I've read, as to who the people are, what has happened and why they are doing what they are doing. <br/><br/>I like the concepts which seem close to Narnia's The Silver Chair - a land of fierce giants, an underground world of tunnels and a small unattractive race. However why are the main characters going there? Once they find themselves be</span>
  <span id="freeText18115615006023357275" style="display:none">I found myself at a severe disadvantage by not having read the earlier book in the fantasy series. No information is presented in the first quarter, which is as far as I've read, as to who the people are, what has happened and why they are doing what they are doing. <br /><br />I like the concepts which seem close to Narnia's The Silver Chair - a land of fierce giants, an underground world of tunnels and a small unattractive race. However why are the main characters going there? Once they find themselves beginning to turn into worms - what a ghastly transmogrification, so well imagined for us! why do they keep walking? <br /><br />In interspersed segments we see a few young people in our world whose relative has died. A man they don't know, comes to state that he is the executor of the estate - I'd be looking for written confirmation and ID, which the relatives don't - but at this point I have no idea how these people connect to the other characters in the city of worms. <br /><br />Various devices are used to catch up a new reader or a previous reader who has forgotten some of the story. These can include conversation among characters, letters, a diary, a dream, a memory recalled for us, internal dialogue of the main character. Lacking these, I'm going to have to wait until I can get the first book and read it, because my interest is definitely piqued but this is not the way to read this second book. Other readers should take note and start at the start. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18115615006023357275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3097906376523323259" style="display:none">Following the first book, The City of Worms brings us in the continuation of the adventures of Owen and his friends in the aftermath of what happened in the previous one. Owen now is faced with Them claiming more power and trying to possess control of The City of Worms in order to win the war of good and evil.   <span id="freeText11840865743624548653" style="display:none">I like the story line author Huff has going in these books. he did do in this book what I thought should have been done in the first. Which is give us a look at Them. Not everything, but a glimpse into motivations other than the basic good/evil thing.<br /><br />That said, the story got weighed down with over-complicated explanations of the layers of his multiverse. One Character, Cleophus, in an advanced stage of dementia is explaining it to the Nine. One character makes an apt observation with the line "This is getting confusing." Couldn't have said it better myself.<br /><br />Owen and The Keeper's battle with the forces of Them is interesting nevertheless. The ending was too simplistic for the set-up as Owen finds the second Pillar of Truth.<br /><br />Promising.</span>

Our main character Owen is constantly put in situations where the faith of his friends and fellow adventures help to give him the courage to get things done and continue to stay true to himself with honesty and integrity.</span>

  <span id="freeText9511267728828793126" style="display:none">I was given an advance copy by the author to review. Although I was leery, as I struggled with the first installment, I dived into the book, readily. There was more background given in this chapter of Owen Sage's story. It also introduced a new race, the Ubaloo, a tiny race of warriors. There is the classic battle of good vs. evil and unexpected twists where one character or another turns traitor. The idea of the worms possessing essence that could change the world was also inventive. I did, however find a lot of repetition and a few minor typos. Nothing that took away from the story, but distracting all the same. All in all it was a much more enjoyable read than the first book. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/z7Up8q38L6KNuEYsnEHh9OsiIBn6ahWipmVQKfUo9YvAywKGZ2d08GzNSxRmgUhvorl0Syxz/hfX8XWAR8bfQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HaPpGBWafMikVKM05EP0H1HuwEckWsZlhrWF+6L5dmjNnhG1xrARpe/RdwAHqPa5PMitFm8CoctTc9VtBDLOww==')})
  }
